  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_949f0976-fee9-415d-931a-04b72b8560c8'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText11801701570471051283" style="display:none">HOW CAN ONE GIRL SAVE AN ENTIRE WORLD?<br /><br />To the nobles who live in Benden Weyr, Lessa is nothing but a ragged kitchen girl. For most of her life she has survived by serving those who betrayed her father and took over his lands. Now the time has come for Lessa to shed her disguise—and take back her stolen birthright. <br /><br />But everything changes when she meets a queen dragon. The bond they share will be deep and last forever. It will protect them when, for the first time in centuries, Lessa’s world is threatened by Thread, an evil substance that falls like rain and destroys everything it touches. Dragons and their Riders once protected the planet from Thread, but there are very few of them left these days. Now brave Lessa must risk her life, and the life of her beloved dragon, to save her beautiful world. . . .</span>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/40962655-karen-kerr"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1425674559i/40962655._UX100_CR0,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/40962655-karen-kerr">Karen Kerr</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I don't think it has "paled" at all. I read it 20 years ago and enjoyed its characters and story, and now just finished reading it again and enjoyed i<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I don't think it has "paled" at all. I read it 20 years ago and enjoyed its characters and story, and now just finished reading it again and enjoyed it on newer levels. The writing is rich and active. No dawdling with useless scenes or words. The introduction is a page and a half - got that? a page and a half! - and you learn from it more information about their history and world than I could put in a comment. The language is so rich you can make a vocab list out of it, yet never feel you didn't get the gist of a line. And Lessa! How can anyone not see how fully developed a character Lessa is? For the year it came out, she was a milestone in the strength of women. She inspired, and continues to inspire. This book absolutely deserved every praise and award it receives.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=all-time-favorites">all-time-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=alpha-male">alpha-male</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=quest">quest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=to-review">to-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer463027008" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6561582100635882673">I understand that this book (and series) has a lot of haters. Their complaints are valid, but I still regard this as one of the best sci-fi fantasies I've ever read. <br/><br/>I started reading this series really young, and got so caught up in the whole "OMG DRAGONS" part of it that I didn't even realize until later that this book had sci-fi elements, namely, that we are on a different freaking planet here. It's a mishmash of several genres that worked surprisingly well.<br/><br/>From the other reviews of the book </span>
  <span id="freeText6561582100635882673" style="display:none">I understand that this book (and series) has a lot of haters. Their complaints are valid, but I still regard this as one of the best sci-fi fantasies I've ever read. <br /><br />I started reading this series really young, and got so caught up in the whole "OMG DRAGONS" part of it that I didn't even realize until later that this book had sci-fi elements, namely, that we are on a different freaking planet here. It's a mishmash of several genres that worked surprisingly well.<br /><br />From the other reviews of the book I've read, the main complaints about the book seems to be the fact that the leading male character is kind of an asshole, of the Jericho-fucking-Barrons sort. Let me tell you that I hate Jericho-fucking-Barrons (come ON, I have a fucking shelf named after him, for Christ's sake). <br /><br />Yes, this book can be conveyed as being misogynistic, but I don't think that's fair to the main characters. F'lar is an asshole at times, but he needs to be tough and a leader. I'm not using that as an excuse, I'm just saying that his character was not over the top, and he is not an asshole for the sake of being an asshole, unlike Jericho-fucking-Barrons.<br /><br />Keep in mind also that this book was published a long time ago (1968!). You have to make reasonable accomodations for that; and this book was pretty well advanced for its days. Lessa, the main female character, may be a bitch at times, but taking into consideration her very difficult background, her behavior is perfectly fitting with her character.<br /><br />However dated it is, this book still has one of the most well-thought out setting I've ever read in fantasy and sci-fi. The dragons and how they came about, the societal structure, the culture, everything was well-written and believable.<br /><br />No, this book is not perfect, but I adored this book and this series.<br /><br />Read this review and more @ <a href="http://thebookeaters.net" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Eaters</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_3211537292" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3211537292" />
    <a title="Merphy Napier" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier"><img alt="Merphy Napier" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1524921716p2/41973734.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3211537292?book_show_action=true">Feb 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Merphy Napier" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Merphy Napier" href="/user/show/41973734-merphy-napier">Merphy Napier</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41973734-merphy-napier?shelf=one-star">one-star</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3211537292" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8046033479605484388">(I'm sorry in advance to everyone who grew up loving this book. I promise you, I really tried to love it too)<br/><br/>What I liked:<br/>- our mc started out great. She was strong, scrappy, sure she was impulsive and rude at times, but it all made sense for where she came from.<br/>- fast paced and easy to read plot<br/>- generally fairly interesting ideas<br/><br/>What I REALLY didn't like:<br/>- most of the characters are very shallow and really not well developed or layered at all.<br/>- the execution of the plot was also really shallow</span>
  <span id="freeText8046033479605484388" style="display:none">(I'm sorry in advance to everyone who grew up loving this book. I promise you, I really tried to love it too)<br /><br />What I liked:<br />- our mc started out great. She was strong, scrappy, sure she was impulsive and rude at times, but it all made sense for where she came from.<br />- fast paced and easy to read plot<br />- generally fairly interesting ideas<br /><br />What I REALLY didn't like:<br />- most of the characters are very shallow and really not well developed or layered at all.<br />- the execution of the plot was also really shallow. Sure, it was fast paced and easy to read, but also NOTHING WENT WRONG! They regularly put themselves in dangerous situations but nothing ever went even slightly wrong. Tension? This author doesn't know her.<br />- set up of the story. (removing this part because a couple people have mentioned that more time had passed between the attacks than I had thought. I apologize for my mistake)<br />(now lets get to what moved this from a low three star all the way down to a one)<br />- the romance. So due the way this world is set up ("dragon sex makes me horny" is what it narrows down to), our mc is boarderline raped. The man who does it even admits to it. <i> "He had not thought to control his dragon-incided emotions, and Lessa's first sexual experience had been violent... He had been a considerate and gentle bedmate ever since, but... he would coax her into responding wholeheartedly to his lovemaking eventually" </i> (page 104) So basically, she's taken away from her home, forced into the experience, sexually assaulted, and then ends up in this really abusive relationship (and it's not just abusive because of the sexual assault)<br />- the love interest. Not only does he sexually assault her, but he also verbally abuses her, and physically assaults her. He constantly degrades and insults her, SHAKES her regularly, and slaps her! What a great guy.<br />- our mc's arc. Lessa's love interest really breaks a lot of her spirit in this book and she generally fears disappointing him because she knows he'll continue assaulting her. Here's some more fun quotes, <i> "Oh, F'lar will be so angry with me. He will shake me and shake me, He always shakes me when I disobey him." "He'll shake me," Lessa cried, like a little girl." </i> (and there's a lot more lines like this). I hear her character grows to be incredibly strong throughout the series. I'm glad to hear that because she deserves it.<br />- MORE ROMANCE MADNESS! Don't worry guys. She grows to love her abuser. So it's romantic.<br /><br />I know a lot of people grew up loving this book. And I think if I had read it at a much younger age, I would have had a great time reading the fast and easy plot. And a lot of this other stuff would have gone over my head. But man, this is a book I'm not passing on to my kids to read.<br /><br />Edit:<br />Obviously this review made a few people mad. it's a well loved story so I get being defensive of it. And I really don't mind people having differing opinions than I do. But keep in mind that just because the book was written in 1968 doesn't mean it's depiction of a romantic relationship can't be viewed with a critical eye.</span>

<div id="review_8907691" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/8907691" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mike" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mike" href="/user/show/545336-mike">Mike</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780345247766" href="/book/show/1132538.Dragonflight">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Nobody</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=xcharity-2011">xcharity-2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/545336-mike?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer8907691" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4498773882584860599">What a disappointment. It started out just fine with Lessa, sole survivor of her family wreaking revenge on the evil dude who conquered "Ruatha Hold". The whole dragon/human mind meld thing was okay too. The part that really disgusted me was the whole raping/physical abuse shtick by the supposed hero. My thoughts were, if this was my daughter as the heroine, then the only thing to be done would "bag and tag" that F'lar a**hole cause I would have invented the .45 cal and then blown his head off w</span>
  <span id="freeText4498773882584860599" style="display:none">What a disappointment. It started out just fine with Lessa, sole survivor of her family wreaking revenge on the evil dude who conquered "Ruatha Hold". The whole dragon/human mind meld thing was okay too. The part that really disgusted me was the whole raping/physical abuse shtick by the supposed hero. My thoughts were, if this was my daughter as the heroine, then the only thing to be done would "bag and tag" that F'lar a**hole cause I would have invented the .45 cal and then blown his head off with it. I don't get why this was important to the storyline, gee abuse the girl long enough and she'll fall for you in the end. Frankly thought it was stupid.<br /><br />Another thing that r'ally ann'yed me was the st'pid ap'strophe w'y to sp'll ev'ryone's friggin' n'mes!!! I want to pour scalding hot <i>klah</i> on the whole bunch.<br /><br />The premise that the world forgets, within a few years, a recurring extraterrestrial threat that destroys entire continents was idiotic. If they really forget the whole technological base that enabled them to defeat the "threads", the whole society deserves to perish. And "threads" are not a very exciting enemy, "wow, look at them falling from the sky in clumps..." <br /><br />Dialogue sucks mostly. Toward the end, there were parts where somebody "roared" with laughter, but I never saw anything remotely funny to cause it.<br /><br />I was really looking forward to a long and interesting series but not here. Good thing I didn't buy any of the follow-on's. I may have a tough time starting some of her other novels I have on the "to-read" list.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4498773882584860599" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_929569602" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929569602" />
    <a title="Markus" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26681101-markus"><img alt="Markus" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1421952301p2/26681101.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/929569602?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Markus" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Markus" href="/user/show/26681101-markus">Markus</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26681101-markus?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer929569602" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14612502687455458024">It always pains me when a beloved classic is just not good enough. <i>Dragonflight</i> by Anne McCaffrey was unfortunately plain unenjoyable.<br/><br/>The setting is the least intriguing one I have been faced with in quite a long time. There was just nothing to pique my interest on the world of Pern. In the author’s defence, she wrote this book in a time when only Tolkien had had the vision and ambition to take a fantasy world to marvellous complexity, and long before the intricacy and skills of the likes of Jor</span>
  <span id="freeText14612502687455458024" style="display:none">It always pains me when a beloved classic is just not good enough. <i>Dragonflight</i> by Anne McCaffrey was unfortunately plain unenjoyable.<br /><br />The setting is the least intriguing one I have been faced with in quite a long time. There was just nothing to pique my interest on the world of Pern. In the author’s defence, she wrote this book in a time when only Tolkien had had the vision and ambition to take a fantasy world to marvellous complexity, and long before the intricacy and skills of the likes of Jordan, Martin, Erikson and Sanderson surfaced to take up the mantle. But I have seen many wonderful worlds in stories from before the current generation, and Pern simply does not measure up.<br /><br />The plot was in my eyes horribly executed. If if was supposed to be exciting, it all happened in the wrong order with the wrong people and nothing ever went wrong; in short, no suspense was created nor any interest sparked, and there was no reason to care about what happened. As for the characters, the most special part about them was the silly overuse of apostrophes in their names.<br /><br /><i>Dragonriders of Pern</i> is inarguably entry level fantasy. That is never a bad thing in itself, and I am sure McCaffrey’s fans have reasons why they enjoy her books. But personally, this is fantasy on a level which I would not recommend to anyone, and I would much rather suggest the heavily criticised <i>Inheritance Cycle</i> (which was partly inspired by this series, but in my eyes is far less overrated).<br /><br />In the end, there was nothing to inspire or excite me in <i>Dragonflight</i>, and not even anything to connect with. The only thing that even slightly interested me was the combination of fantasy and science fiction elements, which we of course see very little of.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14612502687455458024" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13898721462023396079">I cannot imagine why I have never read this before. I have had plenty of time to do so since it was first published in 1968.   <span id="freeText13898721462023396079" style="display:none">I cannot imagine why I have never read this before. I have had plenty of time to do so since it was first published in 1968. It is fantasy/ sci fi, two of my favourite genres. And it has dragons in it! What more could I want?<br />Well I have now read it and I am joining the side of the people who love it! I thought the world building was extremely good and I liked the idea of the threads (some kind of weird fungal growth) periodically falling on the planet and threatening to destroy it. <br />The idea of the Dragonriders being chosen by their baby dragons, probably while they are still in their eggs has certainly been copied a few times. (<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/113436.Eragon__The_Inheritance_Cycle___1_" title="Eragon (The Inheritance Cycle, #1) by Christopher Paolini" rel="nofollow noopener">Eragon</a>?). In fact a lot of her ideas about dragons have probably been copied since 1968:)<br />The characters are well written, dragons as well as humans. Lessa annoyed me a few times by leaping to conclusions and acting without thought but of course the consequences did further the story.<br />Really I am giving it five stars because while I was reading it I was practically living inside the book! I was so involved I was even thinking about it when I was not reading. To me that is always the sign of a really good book. Now on to the next one.............</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10265602401629760922">It should be stated that I squandered most of junior high reading Anne McCaffrey's sci-fi/fantasy novels near-exclusively, but this was my first time revisiting her since then. I was surprised to find that the first book in the <i>Dragonriders of Pern</i> series actually does have a good story, with interesting characters and an excellent invented world. However, the writing is just abominable, and in spite of being a woman, McCaffrey is frustratingly chauvanistic. The (lack of) copyediting makes me cr</span>
  <span id="freeText10265602401629760922" style="display:none">It should be stated that I squandered most of junior high reading Anne McCaffrey's sci-fi/fantasy novels near-exclusively, but this was my first time revisiting her since then. I was surprised to find that the first book in the <i>Dragonriders of Pern</i> series actually does have a good story, with interesting characters and an excellent invented world. However, the writing is just abominable, and in spite of being a woman, McCaffrey is frustratingly chauvanistic. The (lack of) copyediting makes me cry, and the writing is something you just have to suffer through, but the idea is really inventive, and I can totally understand how I got so sucked into her books as a kid. I wouldn't exactly recommend that you run out and check her books out, but if you liked them back in the day, revisiting them isn't as painful as you might have thought it would be.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_57047824" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/57047824" />
    <a title="Brad" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1022982-brad"><img alt="Brad" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442484575p2/1022982.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/57047824?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brad" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brad" href="/user/show/1022982-brad">Brad</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1022982-brad?shelf=sci-fantasy">sci-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer57047824" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17980958341309514527">Lately I have been noticing a recurring observation about the quality of first books in various series. There seems to be a growing consensus in reviews that the first book of a series, particularly if it is the first book published by an author, is inherently weak because the author is "learning their craft."<br/><br/>It seems to be both an excuse for what is perceived as poor quality and an excuse for going on in the series despite being underwhelmed by the opener. <br/><br/>I had this in mind as I began reading </span>
  <span id="freeText17980958341309514527" style="display:none">Lately I have been noticing a recurring observation about the quality of first books in various series. There seems to be a growing consensus in reviews that the first book of a series, particularly if it is the first book published by an author, is inherently weak because the author is "learning their craft."<br /><br />It seems to be both an excuse for what is perceived as poor quality and an excuse for going on in the series despite being underwhelmed by the opener. <br /><br />I had this in mind as I began reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey" title="Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Anne McCaffrey</a>'s <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a>, and for two thirds of the book I thought it was a perfect descriptor of what I was seeing. <br /><br />But once I finished the book, I thought that maybe "the poor opener" isn't always the case (although I willingly concede that this is probably the case more often than not). Perhaps there is something else going on -- especially in something like Dragonflight.<br /><br />Dragonflight is a fast read, and it is sparingly written. We get a taste of the main characters -- F'lar and Mnementh, Lessa and Ramoth, F'nor and Canth -- but we aren't given much time with them, not enough to get to know them deeply. McCaffrey races us through the story, spanning many Turns (the Pernese year) in a very short time. There is a clear goal to her plot -- save Pern from the threat of the Threads -- and McCaffrey is ruthless and expedient in getting us there. <br /><br />I can understand how many readers see this as a narrative failure. After all, we like getting to know characters in the books we read, and we seem to prefer saving our breathless action driven stories for the big screen. <br /><br />If this is our preference, a story which focuses on the latter rather than the former has failed on some level, and that failure is generally considered the writer's failure and, more specifically, a failure of their writing. <br /><br />I wonder, though, if this is always the case. It seems to me that it is just as likely that Dragonflight's quickness could have more to do with the peculiarities of its publishing (it was two novellas squished together to make a novel), the requirements of a first time writer to get their work just right so that it can be published at all (which often means cutting out superfluities), and the tendency of first books to be edited more thoroughly than future books. <br /><br />Once you've become "Anne McCaffrey," for instance, editors tend to step back and give you more room. They let you spend many more ages on character building, and you're given less notes on your work. You are "Anne McCaffrey," best selling author, and you must know what you're doing, so do what you want.<br /><br />Perhaps then, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a> is a product of the necessities of a first novel rather than an example of the author not being polished in her writing skills.<br /><br />All this aside, I appreciated the quickness of the tale. There is something to be said for brevity, and I felt I got enough of the characters. I cared about them without knowing everything, and some of their shabbier behaviours -- such as F'lar's constant physical abuse of Lessa, and Lessa's infuriating capacity for inspired stupidity -- were more tolerable than they might have been if I'd been forced to spend time digging through their psychologies. <br /><br />Of course, this appreciation for skeletal characterization could all be the screenwriter in me (I doubt it, though, since the main complaint about my screenplays by those with the money is that they are too character driven), but that's okay because that informs the kind of reader I can be. Every once in a while I like my stories quick and my characters less defined (although this is far from always the case), and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a> fit that bill right when I needed it most.<br /><br />Regardless, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61975.Dragonflight__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_1_" title="Dragonflight (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonflight</a> was a surprise for me, and I liked it much more than I thought I would. I don't know if I will go on, though. I may just let it stand alone, enjoying its quality as is. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17980958341309514527" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_228632704" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228632704" />
    <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell"><img alt="Sebastien Castell" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1378071485p2/4846758.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228632704?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sebastien Castell" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sebastien Castell" href="/user/show/4846758-sebastien-castell">Sebastien Castell</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4846758-sebastien-castell?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4846758-sebastien-castell?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228632704" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6106884627826210573">It's been ages since I read Dragonflight by Anne McCaffrey. It was my first introduction to her writing and more specifically her world of Pern with its blend of fantasy and sci-fi (everything looks fantasy but is explained – thanks to the ubiquitous prologues across the series – as science fiction.) I rarely re-read books, but felt like going back to something familiar and so thought I'd give Dragonflight a try to see how it has aged in the intervening years.<br/><br/>The first thing that strikes a moder</span>
  <span id="freeText6106884627826210573" style="display:none">It's been ages since I read Dragonflight by Anne McCaffrey. It was my first introduction to her writing and more specifically her world of Pern with its blend of fantasy and sci-fi (everything looks fantasy but is explained – thanks to the ubiquitous prologues across the series – as science fiction.) I rarely re-read books, but felt like going back to something familiar and so thought I'd give Dragonflight a try to see how it has aged in the intervening years.<br /><br />The first thing that strikes a modern reader is how remarkably gendered everything is in that world. Women and men serve very different roles, which sometimes feels so off as to be grating. This didn't surprise me since, even as a teenager, I remembered finding Dragonflight oddly sexist in ways that sometimes felt out of step even with the world as presented in the pages of the book. What I noticed this time was that it was a bit funny how even the dragons get this treatment: gold dragons are vital, matronly forces whose primary function and source of pride is producing large quantities of eggs. Green dragons are . . . well, kind of promiscuous for the hell of it.<br /><br />The women in the books tend towards similar descriptions, either being consumed with the idea of maternal duty or with sleeping with as many dragonriders as possible. There are plenty of exceptions, of course, otherwise the book would descend into self-satire, but the trend feels so consistent as to sometimes make it hard to distinguish between one secondary character and another. More troubling, of course, is the constant shaking of women, the use of physically dominant actions even as modes of affection, and the unclear way in which consent is understood within the world.<br /><br />I'll dispense with this part of the review quickly, since I lack any useful training or qualification for delivering much of an analysis other than, "Geez, it sure seems kinda sexist a lot of the time." I do find it kind of embarrassing to read online the far-reaching justifications for the world of Pern, that so often seek to find some explanation for its preposterously gendered rules beyond the obvious one that Anne McCaffrey just happened to have views about gender that don't fit all that well in our contemporary world. This always seems like the problem with call-out culture, though: if something is popular enough, rationales are constructed by which to grant the author a pass, even when it's the work itself and not the author that we should have the issues with.<br /><br />But why does that desire to preserve the sanctity of McCaffrey's books exist in the first place? Because they're just really good stories. The world of Pern, its peculiar dragons and dragonriders, the economics and politics and social conflicts that emerge from the threat of spores that periodically come from the sky, destroying everything in their path, makes for interesting reading even decades later. It's worth noting that Dragonsong, McCaffrey's third book set in this world, remains my favourite children's book of all time and though I have nothing demographically in common with Menolly these days, I still have no difficulty seeing the world of Pern through her eyes and sharing in her adventures.<br /><br />It's also worth noting that even in Dragonflight, Lessa, the main character of the book, has loads of agency despite the highly gendered world she lives in. I wouldn't go so far as to say she challenges those roles, but certainly she chooses to interpret them in her own way despite the resistance she gets from everyone around her.<br /><br />All of this confuses and conspires to make Dragonflight a mixed bag for me. The quality of storytelling seems undeniable, and even the problematic aspects of the book are sometimes confounded by McCaffrey's own narrative choices. At first I thought the sexist aspects were just my present, much older self reading with the voices of online outrage culture shouting in my head, but as the book went along I remembered that all these elements struck me as troubling even as a teenage boy.<br /><br />I suppose all that leaves to say is this: Dragonflight is a good book, and one fantasy and sci-fi fans who haven't yet journeyed to Pern for the first time are likely to enjoy, even as they may find themselves staring curiously at the pages, wondering why it was so damned important that women fit into such narrow roles.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6106884627826210573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6223057277305902603">I read this book back in sixth grade and thought it was exciting in the "wow, dragons are so cool; I wish I had one!" sense. I read it again on a whim and found it unintentionally disturbing. It's not just that the writing seemed dry and the characterization wooden. I realize the book was written in the late 60's, but the male-female dynamics still seem uncomfortably dated. The text seems to condone F'lar's treatment of Lessa; he patronizes her, yells at her, shakes her when he's angry, and prac</span>
  <span id="freeText6223057277305902603" style="display:none">I read this book back in sixth grade and thought it was exciting in the "wow, dragons are so cool; I wish I had one!" sense. I read it again on a whim and found it unintentionally disturbing. It's not just that the writing seemed dry and the characterization wooden. I realize the book was written in the late 60's, but the male-female dynamics still seem uncomfortably dated. The text seems to condone F'lar's treatment of Lessa; he patronizes her, yells at her, shakes her when he's angry, and practically rapes her. She never confronts him about it. And then, plot aside, she's supposed to "come around" to love him in the end. I never noticed it when I was younger, but it troubles me now that this is supposed to feel romantic.<br /></span>

<div id="review_54622660" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/54622660" />
    <a title="Libby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1803452-libby"><img alt="Libby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1248364924p2/1803452.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=fantasy-fairytale-and-myth">fantasy-fairytale-and-myth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=fantasy-epic-and-series">fantasy-epic-and-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1803452-libby?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer54622660" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13811940740971081333">I truly enjoyed this book and am looking forward to continuing with the series. This work is a well-written, creative adventure novel with the perfect amount of romance. It’s storytelling at its best. <br/><br/>The book is a nice mix of Science Fiction and Fantasy. The setting is the world of Pern. We are told in the Prologue that Pern is a planet settled by Earthlings but now long forgotten. It has apparently reverted back to a feudal type society where most of the citizens live in “holds” which are hist</span>
  <span id="freeText13811940740971081333" style="display:none">I truly enjoyed this book and am looking forward to continuing with the series. This work is a well-written, creative adventure novel with the perfect amount of romance. It’s storytelling at its best. <br /><br />The book is a nice mix of Science Fiction and Fantasy. The setting is the world of Pern. We are told in the Prologue that Pern is a planet settled by Earthlings but now long forgotten. It has apparently reverted back to a feudal type society where most of the citizens live in “holds” which are historically protected by “Weyrs”. The biggest threat facing Pern is environmental; the Threads fall from a neighboring planet and destroy all organic matter on Pern. For centuries the Dragonmen, residents of the Weyrs, have used their dragons to sear the Threads out of the sky before they can infect Pern. But now, over 400 years have passed without any Threads falling and the people of Pern believe the danger is over and that the Dragonmen have outlived their purpose. Too late, we find out that failing to maintain and believe in tradition has weakened the people of Pern and there are dire consequences when the Threads return.<br /><br />I’ve seen a lot of criticism here that the book lacks character development and/or that the main romantic relationship is sexist and abusive etc. I do agree that this book is somewhat dated and that how writers represent romantic relationships has certainly altered to reflect the current social norms. However, I think the romantic relationship between F’lar and Lessa, while dated, is not outright abusive. As the setting of the book is feudal, I think the male dominate culture is appropriate. Further, much of this resolves as you see their relationship evolve over the course of the book into a relationship of equals. All that aside, this is a Sci/Fi / Fantasy novel not a dating manual. I find it odd that readers expect to see healthy, politically correct relationships and/or that they expect people to emulate the relationships they read about in books; if that’s true so much for Wuthering Heights. The relationship fits the setting and works for the novel. I think people may read too much into it. <br /><br />The highlight of this book for me is the amazing relationship between a rider and his/her dragon. Once a dragon Impresses a rider they are forever two parts of one whole. The relationship is unique and moving. It’s a great companion aspect to the fast paced and engaging plot. I’d recommend this to anyone who enjoys a book that is a lighter read while still being a richly told adventure story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13811940740971081333" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3435584947" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <span id="freeText18428987457767723830" style="display:none">The start of a well-known series. It is dragon-centric, so heavy with dragon-lore and dragon-activities and dragon-relationships and dragony stuff that it left me curious about the characters.<br /><br />For all of its world building, threads and mind-tapping, and so forth, it fell rather flat for me. <div id="review_857709734" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/857709734" />
    <a title="Alexa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa"><img alt="Alexa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1408028716p2/17295220.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/857709734?book_show_action=true">Feb 17, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alexa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alexa" href="/user/show/17295220-alexa">Alexa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17295220-alexa?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer857709734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5451700231498633225">Around 2.5 stars. <br/><br/><b>This book's prologue is terrible. </b><br/><br/>It's an opening narration supposed to serve (as they usually do) as an introduction to the story. However, it feels like an unnecessary info dump, placed there because apparently readers are too stupid to figure stuff out on their own and need to be spoon fed all the important facts.<br/><br/>From then on things weren't <i>that</i> bad. The story is easy to read and I found the mix of Sci Fi/Fantasy really interesting. But the plot has holes and coincidences an</span>
  <span id="freeText5451700231498633225" style="display:none">Around 2.5 stars. <br /><br /><b>This book's prologue is terrible. </b><br /><br />It's an opening narration supposed to serve (as they usually do) as an introduction to the story. However, it feels like an unnecessary info dump, placed there because apparently readers are too stupid to figure stuff out on their own and need to be spoon fed all the important facts.<br /><br />From then on things weren't <i>that</i> bad. The story is easy to read and I found the mix of Sci Fi/Fantasy really interesting. But the plot has holes and coincidences and ex-machina moments everywhere... I lost count of the times when I said: <i>"That should have gone wrong."</i> It never did.<br /><br />One of the things that bothered me the most was the absence of female characters. Actually, the absence of females. The dragonriders live with a group of people that supports them, and most of the riders come from the boys these families have. Now, unless otherwise stated, probability of having a girl or a boy is 50/50, which means there should be as many girls as boys in the weyr. However, when they need a dragonwoman or whatever the name was, they have to go search the outside world for girls... What happened to the ones they should have had in the Weyr? No one knows.<br /><br />Overall it wasn't as bad as other "classics" of the genre that I have read, but I don't think I'll be continuing with the series. <br /><br />Also, let it be known that ad'ding stu'pid apostrophes eve'rywhere doesn't make your nam'es more interes'ting. :/<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5451700231498633225" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_576058030" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/576058030" />
    <a title="David Sven" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven"><img alt="David Sven" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402220807p2/8802423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/576058030?book_show_action=true">Mar 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David Sven" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David Sven" href="/user/show/8802423-david-sven">David Sven</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6327222-dragonflight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8802423-david-sven?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer576058030" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3473104292638694233">A quick and easy read. The world building is light with a lot of unanswered questions, but I'm assured that the series as a whole "fills out" in that regard. I enjoyed it.<br/><br/>The prologue had me doing a double take because it was pure scifi, with Pern being one of many colonised planets which eventually became isolated and forgotten by Earth. The technology then regressed to the more fantasy feel medieval style setting. There are dragons, but even these are indigenous animals that have been bred to </span>
  <span id="freeText3473104292638694233" style="display:none">A quick and easy read. The world building is light with a lot of unanswered questions, but I'm assured that the series as a whole "fills out" in that regard. I enjoyed it.<br /><br />The prologue had me doing a double take because it was pure scifi, with Pern being one of many colonised planets which eventually became isolated and forgotten by Earth. The technology then regressed to the more fantasy feel medieval style setting. There are dragons, but even these are indigenous animals that have been bred to resemble dragons of Earth mythology. There's no magic per se. Rather we have dragons with the ability to teleport and certain human blood lines are able to telepathically communicate and "bond" with the dragons.<br /><br />The dragons are bred to combat an invasion of "Threads," a life destroying "entity" or "organism" that travels from Pern's sister planet every two hundred years when the planets are closest in their orbits.<br /><br /><br />The story is set when there has been 400 years of no "Threads" and the dragons have been in decline. As the 200 year cycle comes around once more the queen dragon is dying and a new "Weyrwoman" is sought to bond with a new queen dragon before the "Threads" fall once again.<br /><br />It held my attention from start to finish. I'll probably read the next book in the series when I need a quick palate cleanser.<br /><br /><br />4 stars</span>
  <a data-text-id="3473104292638694233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_17575471" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17575471" />
    <a title="Sean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/138600-sean"><img alt="Sean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562511132p2/138600.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17575471?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sean" href="/user/show/138600-sean">Sean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/138600-sean?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17575471" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer674020434801037708">The Dragonriders of Pern series really caught my imagination back in my preteen/early-teen years, when I picked up a library copy of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20082.The_Renegades_of_Pern___7___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__' title='The Renegades of Pern (#7) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Renegades of Pern</a> that my mom had put down. I next read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61926.All_The_Weyrs_Of_Pern' title='All The Weyrs Of Pern by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>All the Weyrs of Pern</a> (thrilling at the brilliant cover art by Michael Whelan) and then started from the beginning, whipping through Dragonflight, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127584.Dragonquest__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_2_' title='Dragonquest (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 2) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonquest</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_3_' title='The White Dragon (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 3) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The White Dragon</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_4_' title='Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 4) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moreta</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61974.Nerilka_s_Story___5___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__' title='Nerilka's Story (#5) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nerilka's Story</a> and the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28541.Dragonsong__Harper_Hall_Trilogy__Book_1_' title='Dragonsong (Harper Hall Trilogy, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Harper Hall Trilogy</a>.<br/><br/>I recently had the urge to revisit those carefree years of meaningless scienc</span>
  <span id="freeText674020434801037708" style="display:none">The Dragonriders of Pern series really caught my imagination back in my preteen/early-teen years, when I picked up a library copy of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20082.The_Renegades_of_Pern___7___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__" title="The Renegades of Pern (#7) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Renegades of Pern</a> that my mom had put down. I next read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61926.All_The_Weyrs_Of_Pern" title="All The Weyrs Of Pern by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">All the Weyrs of Pern</a> (thrilling at the brilliant cover art by Michael Whelan) and then started from the beginning, whipping through Dragonflight, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127584.Dragonquest__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_2_" title="Dragonquest (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 2) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonquest</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_3_" title="The White Dragon (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 3) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">The White Dragon</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Dragonriders_of_Pern__Book_4_" title="Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Dragonriders of Pern, Book 4) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Moreta</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61974.Nerilka_s_Story___5___Dragonriders_of_Pern__Paperback__" title="Nerilka's Story (#5) (Dragonriders of Pern (Paperback)) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Nerilka's Story</a> and the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/28541.Dragonsong__Harper_Hall_Trilogy__Book_1_" title="Dragonsong (Harper Hall Trilogy, Book 1) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Harper Hall Trilogy</a>.<br /><br />I recently had the urge to revisit those carefree years of meaningless science fiction I enjoyed, and I picked the first three books up again, only to be shocked at how misogynistic, outdated and just plain badly written they were. I mean, I knew they were pulpy, guilty-pleasure-type stuff, but to create a strong female character like Lessa (psi powers! rides a dragon! stubborn! intelligent(?)!) and then pair her with F'lar, who treats her like a child, shakes her when she displeases him . . . and have them fall in love? What kind of nonsense is this?<br /><br />The problem is, as viciously sub-par as her prose, characterization and plotting are, McCaffrey's premise still enthralls me. Even though the idea of any number of dragons being able to keep the skies of an entire continent free of what amounts to a corrosive blizzard is thoroughgoing twaddle, I still can't stop thinking about it. Is an unwilling re-reading of <i>Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</i> in my future??</span>
  <a data-text-id="674020434801037708" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/121100743?book_show_action=true">Sep 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Vivian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Vivian" href="/user/show/3947172-vivian">Vivian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3947172-vivian?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer121100743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7968772124085016938">10/2014 Buddy Reread: Reliving my preteen years with Don<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>Once relieved of imminent danger, Pern settled into a more comfortable way of life. The descendants of heroes fell into disfavor, as the legends fell into disrepute.</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/>Hooray! This book was as good as I remembered. The Pern books had a huge influence on my preadolescent self and I was a little nervous about rereading it and finding out that it wasn't as good. Afraid that it would destroy the related memories I made while reading these stor</span>
  <span id="freeText7968772124085016938" style="display:none">10/2014 Buddy Reread: Reliving my preteen years with Don<br /><br /><b>
  <blockquote>Once relieved of imminent danger, Pern settled into a more comfortable way of life. The descendants of heroes fell into disfavor, as the legends fell into disrepute.</blockquote>
</b><br /><br />Hooray! This book was as good as I remembered. The Pern books had a huge influence on my preadolescent self and I was a little nervous about rereading it and finding out that it wasn't as good. Afraid that it would destroy the related memories I made while reading these stories. Best part, it felt like I was with my father again.<br /><br />Totally forgot how much of a pistol-whip Lessa was. Holy crackers. Headstrong, temperamental and willing to sacrifice herself and others to achieve a goal. Plus, a nice wide streak of vengeance runs through her. She's capable and don't f@#K with her. <br /><br />Glad to say, F'lar and F'nor were still the heartthrobs I recalled. While I respect F'lar's leadership and dedication, his interpersonal habits would drive me nuts. F'nor on the other hand, is so close to a perfect male for me that I still idolize him. <br /><br />The dragons. Mnementh... *deep sigh* If one could love a dragon, then this would be The One. Clever, loyal, acerbic wit and practically perfect in every way. Probably my favorite character in the story. <br /><br />Loved the revenge, Lessa's intrepidness, the mating flight, the harper ballads, and the politics of Pern. I adored Masterharper Robinton's scathing speech at the assembly--definitely need to reread the Harper Hall trilogy. F'lar maneuverings were brilliant and F'nor's loyalty and support--sexy. <b>
  <blockquote>"I don’t object to being . . . importuned, but there are limits to what a man is willing to do out of loyalty to dragon kind.”</blockquote>
</b><br />Still a great adventure story and I wish I could find transport to Pern. <br /><br />Favorite quote:<b>
  <blockquote>“By the Egg, it’s die slow, doing nothing, or die quick, trying."</blockquote>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="7968772124085016938" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_17379168" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/17379168" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/978552-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604572841p2/978552.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/17379168?book_show_action=true">Mar 09, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/978552-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780552084536" href="/book/show/61976.Dragonflight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/978552-cathy?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/978552-cathy?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer17379168" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11550309157172850987">Why is this one of my favourite fantasy series of all time? Sentient dragons, talking telepathically to their riders. People fighting the good fight on dragonback. A really cool world. Entertaining story telling. This is really fun to read. Eat your heart out, Christoper Paolini!<br/><br/>The first 150 pages are a lot of set-up and world building. I can live with that in such a long running series. The romance is mostly non-existent. They meet, they become a pair due to external circumstances, they seem t</span>
  <span id="freeText11550309157172850987" style="display:none">Why is this one of my favourite fantasy series of all time? Sentient dragons, talking telepathically to their riders. People fighting the good fight on dragonback. A really cool world. Entertaining story telling. This is really fun to read. Eat your heart out, Christoper Paolini!<br /><br />The first 150 pages are a lot of set-up and world building. I can live with that in such a long running series. The romance is mostly non-existent. They meet, they become a pair due to external circumstances, they seem to be fond of each other eventually and maybe in love and definitely possessive.<br /><br />I can‘t say how many times I have read this series. Pretty much constantly as a teenager. Unfortunately I do not have my old paperbacks anymore, I gave them all away 25 years ago, when I moved. This is the first re-read since then. And it is definitely the very first time I am reading it in the original English. And now there are some additional books that I have never read.<br /><br />So, Dragonflight—The fun truly starts for me, when Robinton shows up. He is one of my favourite characters of the series. The three Harperhall books are my favourite story arc as well. But first there is this, the beginning of the Dragonriders of Pern.<br /><br />I have questions now that I didn‘t ask in the early 80s, when I read this for the first time. <br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[One is the shaking thing. What is with that? F‘lar pretty much expects Lessa to obey him without question and likes to shake her into submission, when she doesn‘t. Ok, there is an instance of affectionate shaking as well. Whatever that is supposed to be. How Lessa didn‘t develop whiplash remains a mystery.<br /><br />Everybody seems committed to not telling her anything of importance. I am not sure why they don‘t talk with each other and explain things to her like she is an adult. I guess this was McCaffrey‘s way of creating <i>drama</i> suspense. <br /><br />Then there is the pink elephant in the room: lack of consent. Whatever happens, takes place in the off and is not explicit or ever discussed in more depth. One presumes that consent wasn‘t given. Did it bother me as a teenager? No. <br />Would it be considered rape in the present? Yes, probably. Hard to say without actually being in the scene. It does sound like it though. <br />Does the character that took that action feel remorse? Yes, however he had no choice in the matter of the act. But he could have forewarned his wronged counterpart. Guilty by omission. <br />Did it bother me massively in the course of reading the story now? No again. I am still debating that with myself. I guess nostalgia won. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />If this had been my first read, I might have given it three stars. Or 3.5 stars, rounded up? Anyway, nostalgia demands 4 stars, despite the above. Yes, I will read Dragonquest and The White Dragon.<br /><br />————<br />Comments from 2013-ish...?<br /><br />A Dragonriders of Pern re-read on Tor, very tempting.... just came across this entry of a latter part of the book: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.tor.com/2019/04/10/the-constraints-of-time-travel-dragonflight-part-four/">https://www.tor.com/2019/04/10/the-co...</a><br /><br />I am so tempted to read this again. I am a little scared that I wouldn’t like it anymore!<br />————<br />Old non-review:<br />This is a re-read, yet again. I read and re-read the whole series many times over as a teenager and loved it to pieces. Every now and then I read one of them again, mostly for nostalgic value. I still love them. Must-read for all lovers of fantasy and dragonlore.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11550309157172850987" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_187497115" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/187497115" />
    <a title="Jerry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry"><img alt="Jerry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520438201p2/5855981.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/187497115?book_show_action=true">Jul 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jerry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jerry" href="/user/show/5855981-jerry">Jerry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer187497115" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6953348549393000396">Anne McCaffrey, who sadly passed away some years ago, has long been heralded as one of the queens of science fiction and fantasy. Her short story "The Smallest Dragonboy" has even found its way into middle school literature textbooks. <i>Dragonflight</i> is the first entry in her insanely-long <i>Pern</i> series, and felt like a television series premiere in many ways, good and bad. The story was compelling, the writing was mostly good (though there are a few rough spots), and it made for good interplanetary </span>
  <span id="freeText6953348549393000396" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey, who sadly passed away some years ago, has long been heralded as one of the queens of science fiction and fantasy. Her short story "The Smallest Dragonboy" has even found its way into middle school literature textbooks. <i>Dragonflight</i> is the first entry in her insanely-long <i>Pern</i> series, and felt like a television series premiere in many ways, good and bad. The story was compelling, the writing was mostly good (though there are a few rough spots), and it made for good interplanetary fun. However, there were some troublesome parts, and not just the aforementioned "rough spots"; though the book was good as a whole, it still needed some work. Let's hope that the late Ms. McCaffrey improved in her writing ability as time went on.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6953348549393000396" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_51240082" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/51240082" />
    <a title="Diane" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2183662-diane"><img alt="Diane" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1586729383p2/2183662.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/51240082?book_show_action=true">Apr 02, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Diane" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Diane" href="/user/show/2183662-diane">Diane</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2183662-diane?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2183662-diane?shelf=sffbc-book-shelf">sffbc-book-shelf</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2183662-diane?shelf=diane-s-meager-effort">diane-s-meager-effort</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer51240082" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12723880174052667955">I read this first in a pre-GR era, 21 years ago, to be exact. I loved it then and looking back at my records I see that I read most of the series within 2 years. <br/><br/>Now rereading it as a much more mature person, I find that it is just as fun but I noticed certain odd things this time around. Most notably F’lar’s behavior towards Lessa, which is quite overbearing and possessive, right from the get-go, bordering on a rapist’s thoughts and behavior, which he barely manages to rein in. And what’s with </span>
  <span id="freeText12723880174052667955" style="display:none">I read this first in a pre-GR era, 21 years ago, to be exact. I loved it then and looking back at my records I see that I read most of the series within 2 years. <br /><br />Now rereading it as a much more mature person, I find that it is just as fun but I noticed certain odd things this time around. Most notably F’lar’s behavior towards Lessa, which is quite overbearing and possessive, right from the get-go, bordering on a rapist’s thoughts and behavior, which he barely manages to rein in. And what’s with the shaking? He tries to shake “sense” into her. That said, these episodes are extremely brief (just a line or 2) and easily glossed over in a breathless first read. <br /><br />I noticed more of the SF elements this time around having already read the prequel that spells it out. I can now see how she could claim that it was always conceived as SF, where before my reread I didn’t believe it. Those elements are so brief and understated as to be unnoticeable the first time around. <br /><br />I still think these books hold up after so many years because the world-building, the backstory and the plot itself is quite rich. McCaffrey’s writing style is also quite enjoyable to read. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12723880174052667955" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
